[Atharvan.тАФс╣гaс╕Нviс╣Е┼Ыam. k─Б┼Ыyapeyam uta sarv─Бrс╣гaс╣Б ch─Бndasam. tr─Бiс╣гс╣нubham: 2, 3. pan╠Дkti (3. ─Бst─Бrapan╠Дkti); 4, 5, 23, 25, [26]. anuс╣гс╣нubh; 8, 11, 12, 22. jagat─л; 9. bhurij; 14. 4p. atijagat─л.]

Whitney

Comment

Found also (except vss. 19, 20) in P─Бipp. xvi. тМКwith vs. 23 after vs. 24тМЛ. The K─Бu┼Ы. takes no notice of the hymn; тМКbut the V─Бit. (33. 8) allows the use of 21 vss. (from vs. 6 to the end) in the sattra sacrifice at the celebrant’s optionтМЛ.

Translations

Translated: Ludwig, p. 439; Henry, 26, 65; Griffith, i. 416.тАФSee also Muir, v. 370.

Griffith

An enunciation of cosmogonical, ritual, and metrical doctrine

режрез рдХреБрддрд╕реНрддреМ рдЬрд╛рддреМ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Whence [were] those two born? which side (├бrdha) was that? out of
    what world? out of which earth? the two young (vats├б) of the vir─Б╠Бj
    rose out of the sea (salil├б); of those I ask thee: by whether [of
    them was] she milked?
Notes

The ‘which’ is both times katama, implying the existence of more than
two; but Ppp. has instead katarasy─Бс╕е pс╣Ыihivy─Бс╕е.

Griffith

Whence were these two produced? which was that region?’ From what world, from which earth had they their being? Calves of Viraj, these two arose from water. I ask thee of these twain, who was their milker.

Translation
  1. He who caused the sea to resound (krand) with greatness, making a
    threefold lair (y├│ni) as he lay, the desire-milking young of the

tyabhijaс╣Б ┼Ыay─Бnaс╣Б.

Griffith

He who prepared a threefold home, and lying there made the water bellow through his greatness, Calf of Viraj, giving each wish fulfilment, made bodies for him- self far off, in secret.

Translation
  1. What three great ones (bс╣Ыh├бt, n.) there are, the fourth of which
    [one] disjoins [as] speechтАФthe priest (brahm├бn) may know it by
    penance, the inspired one, in which one (├йkam) is joined, in which one
    [is joined].
Notes

Ppp. reads catv─Бri instead of tr─лс╣Зi in a. Caturth├бm ‘fourth’
might also be subject of ‘disjoins.’ Compare ix. 10. 27 (RV. i. 164.
45).

Griffith

Which are the three, the mighty three, whereof the fourth divides the voice, This may the Brahman know by prayer and fervour, whereto belongs the one, whereto the other.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Forth out of bс╣Ыh├бt [as] sixth five s─Бmans [were] fashioned;
    bс╣Ыh├бt was fashioned out of bс╣Ыhat─л╠Б; out of what was bс╣Ыhat─л╠Б made?
Notes

Ppp. reads с╣гaс╣гс╣нhaс╕е instead of -с╣нh─Бt.

Griffith

Out of the Brihat as the sixth five Salmons have been fashioned forth: From Brihati was Brihat formed: whence was the Brihati com- posed?

режрел рдмреГрд╣рддреА рдкрд░рд┐ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Bс╣Ыhat─л╠Б the measure (m─Б╠Бtr─Б) was fashioned forth out of measure
    [as] a mother; illusion (m─Бy─Б╠Б) was born from illusion, M─Бtal─л out of
    illusion.
Notes

The desire to play upon the root m─Б ‘measure, fashion,’ is the leading
motive in the making of this verse. The pada-text gives the absurd
reading m─Бy─Б╠Бс╕е at beginning of c; Ppp. reads after it hi instead
of ha.

Griffith

On measure Brihati is based, and measure on the measurer: From magic might came magic might, from magic might came Matali.

Translation
  1. V─Бi┼Ыv─Бnara’s counterpart [is] the sky above, as far as Agni forced
    (b─Бdh) apart the two firmaments; from that sixth yonder come the
    s├│mas; up from here they go unto the sixth of the day.
Notes

For ─Б╠Б тАЩm├║to, in c, Ppp. reads ─Бmico. The remainder of the hymn,
from this verse on, is by V─Бit. 33. 8 allowed to be introduced at
pleasure in the navar─Бtra ceremony.

Griffith

Vaisvanara’s image is the sky above us, so far as Agni forced both spheres asunder. Thence from that region as the sixth come praise-songs, and every sixth day hence again go upward.

Translation
  1. We these six seers ask thee, O Ka┼Ыyapa, for thou didst join what is
    joined and what is to be joined; they call (ah) vir─Б╠Бj the father of
    the br├бhman; distribute (? vi-dh─Б) it to us [thy] friends
    according to [our] numbers.
Notes

Ppp. reads pс╣Ыch─Бmi с╣Ыс╣г- in a.

Griffith

We, Kagyapa! six present Rishis, ask thee–for thou hast prov- ed things tried and meet for trial They call Viraj the Father of Devotion: tell her to us thy friends in all her figures.

Whitney
Translation
  1. After whom, when removed, the sacrifices remove (pra-cyu),
    [whom], when attending, they attend on (upa-sth─Б), in whose course
    (vrat├б) тМКand?тМЛ impulse the monster (? yakс╣г├б) stirsтАФthat, O seers, is
    the vir─Б╠Бj in the highest firmament.
Notes
Griffith

She whom, advancing, sacrifices follow, and when she takes her station stand beside her, By whose control and hest the spirit moveth, she is Viraj, in highest heaven, O Rishis.

Translation
  1. Breathless, she goes by the breath of breathing ones (f.); vir─Б╠Бj
    goes unto svar─Б╠Бj from behind; vir─Б╠Бj that touches, that is adapted
    to, everythingтАФsome see her, some see her not.
Notes

No ms. тМКof oursтМЛ inserts t between -r─Б╠Бс╣н and sva- in b тМКbut
four of SPP’s do soтМЛ, as required by Pr─Бt. ii. 8 (under which this is
one of the passages quoted). In d we ought properly to have emended
to tve…tve (accentless); all the mss. accent the two words, against
the uniform usage elsewhere; and the pada-mss. commit the further
blunder of giving both times tv├й ├нti, as if the word were the Vedic
locative of the 2d pers. pronoun (as in v. 2. 3).

Griffith

Breathless, she moves by breath of living creatures, Svaraj pre- cedes, Viraj comes closely after. Some men behold her not, and some behold her, Viraj meet- shaped, who thinks of all existence.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Who understandeth (pra-vid) the pair-ness of vir─Б╠Бj? who the
    seasons, who the ordering (k├бlpa) of her? who her steps (kr├бma), how
    many times milked out (vi-duh)? who her abode (dh─Б╠Бman), how many
    times dawnings (vy├╣с╣гс╣нi)?
Notes

The version is much more literal than intelligent, especially at the
end, where we expect rather vy├╣с╣гс╣нam than -с╣н─лs. ‘Pair-ness,’
mithunatv├бm, means especially the condition of being a pair of
opposite sexes.

Griffith

Who hath perceived Viraj’s duplication, perceived her seasons and her rule and practice? Who knows her steps, how oft, how far extended, who knows her home and number of her dawnings?

Whitney
Translation
  1. This same is she that first shone forth; among these other ones (f.)
    she goes about having entered; great mightinesses [are] within her;
    the woman, the new-going generatrix, hath conquered.
Notes

This verse occurred above, as iii. 10. 4. It is found also in other
texts in connection with the four verses which follow it here. Ppp. has
тМКin a, bтМЛ the same readings as in iii. 10. тМК4 a, bтМЛ; тМКand, here
also, it inverts the order of c and dтМЛ.

Griffith

She here who first of all sent forth her lustre moves onward resting on these lower creatures. Exalted power and might are stored within her: the woman hath prevailed, the new-come mother.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The two meter-winged dawns, greatly adorning themselves, move on
    together toward the same lair (y├│ni); spouses of the sun, they move on
    together, understanding, having ensigns, unaging, having abundant seed.
Notes

The Pet. Lexx. give the first word in the form ch├бndaspakс╣гa, although
Pr─Бt. ii. 62 expressly requires -aс╕еpa-, and all the mss. read it
except Bp., which has -aс╣гpa-. The verse is found also in TS. iv. 3.
11┬╣, MS. ii. 13. 10, K. xxxix. 10. Both TS. and MS. have at the
beginning ch├бndasvat─л; MS. reads uс╣г├бs─Бu, and at the end -retas─Бu;
at end of b, MS. gives anus├бс╣Бcarete and TS. ├бnu saс╣Бc├бrant─л; both
have v├н for s├бm in c, and TS. ket├║с╣Б kс╣Ыс╣Зv─Бn├й for ketum├бt─л in
d. Ppp. reads carati in c.

Griffith

Both Dawns on wings of song, with rich adornment, move on together to their common dwelling. Surya’s two wives, unwasting, most prolific, knowing their way, move, rich in light, together.

Translation
  1. Three (f.) have come along the road of righteousness; three heats
    (gharm├б) have come after the seed; one (f.) enlivens the progeny, one
    the refreshment (┼л╠Бrj); one defends the realm of the godly ones.

has r├йtas─Б and TS. jy├│tiс╣г─Б; TS. gives r├бkс╣гati for j├нnvati in
c; and for r─Бс╣гс╣нr├бm in d TS. has vrat├бm and MS. kс╣гatr├бm.

Griffith

The three have passed along the path of Order–three warm libations have regarded offspring One quickens progeny, one strengthens vigour, and one protects the kingdom of the pious.

Whitney
Translation
  1. She that was fourth set Agni-and-Soma; the seers arranging the (two)
    wings of the sacrificeтАФg─Бyatr─л╠Б, triс╣гс╣н├║bh, j├бgat─л, anuс╣гс╣н├║bh, bс╣Ыhadark─л╠Б,
    bringing heaven (sv├аr) for the sacrificer.
Notes

The meter-names in the second half-verse are all in the accusative,
possibly as coordinate with ‘wings’ in b; but comparison with the
other texts indicates that the verse is very corrupt. The translation
implies emendation of adadhus to adadh─Бt in a; it would not be
absolutely impossible to take ’the seers’ as subject in a, and ‘her
that was fourth’ as joint object with ‘Agni-and-Soma.’ Of the other
texts (as above), TS. begins with catuс╣гс╣нom├│ abhavad, and MS. with
catuс╣гс╣нom├бm adadh─Б; both rectify the meter of a by omitting ─Б╠Бs─лt;
in b both have с╣Ыс╣гayas as vocative, and after it bh├бvant─л, and
MS. has pakс╣г─Б╠Б (for -с╣г─Б├║) before it; in c, MS. has vir─Б╠Бjam for
anuс╣гс╣н├║bham; in d, TS. begins with bс╣Ыh├бd ark├бm, MS. with ark├бm
alone; and both follow it with yu├▒j─Бn─Б╠Бс╕е sv├аr (TS., of course, s├║var)
─Б╠Б тАЩbharann id├бm. Ppp’s only variant is bс╣Ыhadark─лr in d.

Griffith

She who was fourth was made by Agni, Soma, and Rishis as. they formed both halves of worship, Gayatri, Trishtup, Jagati, Anushtup, Brihadarki lightening the sacrificer.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Five milkings after five dawnings; five seasons after the five-named
    cow; five quarters arranged by the fifteenthтАФthose (f.) [are]
    one-headed toward one world.
Notes

‘The fifteenth’ (masc. or neut. sing.) might mean also ‘fifteen-fold, of
fifteen parts,’ etc. The verse is found in the three other texts (as
above), but in TS.MS. (also in K.?) separated at some distance from
those that here precede; also in PGS. iii. 3. 5: all read
sam─Бn├бm┼лrdhn─лs instead of ├йkam┼л- in d.

Griffith

Five milkings answer to the fivefold dawning, five seasons to the cow who bears five titles. The five sky-regions made fifteen in number, one head have these to one sole world directed.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Six [are] born the beings first-born of righteousness; six
    s─Б╠Бmans carry the six-day (?) [sacrifice]; after the six-yoked plough
    (s─л╠Бra) severally a s─Б╠Бman; six they call (ah) the heavens and
    earths, six the wide [spaces].

Griffith

Six Elements arose, first-born of Order: the six-day time is carried by six Samans. Six-yoked the plough is, as each trace is numbered: they call both broad ones six; six, Earth and Heaven.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Six they call the cold, and six the hot months; tell ye us the
    season, which one [is] in excess (├бtirikta); seven eagles
    (suparс╣З├б), poets, sat down; seven meters after seven consecrations.
Notes

None of the mss. read ┼Ы─лt─Б╠Бnс╣н с╣г├бс╕Н in a, as demanded by Pr─Бt. ii. 9.
In d the construction of the two nouns is reversible.

Griffith

They call the cold months six, and six the hot ones. Which, tell us, of the seasons is redundant? Seven sages, eagles, have sat down together: seven metres match the seven Consecrations.

  • рдХрд╢реНрдпрдкрдГ, рд╕рдорд╕реНрддрд╛рд░реНрд╖рдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрджрд╛рдВрд╕рд┐, рдЛрд╖рд┐рдЧрдгрдГ

Whitney
Translation
  1. Seven [are] the offerings (h├│ma), the fuels seven, the sweet
    things (m├бdhu, n.) seven, the seasons seven; seven sacrificial butters
    (─Б╠Бjya) went about the existent thing (bh┼лt├б); those (f .) are
    seven-vultured, so have we heard.
Notes

The version is as literal as possible; to modify it would imply an
understanding of it. The nearest fem. word for ’those’ in d to
relate to is ‘fuels’ in a. All the saс╣Бhit─Б-mss. combine sapt├б
rt├бvo in b. Ppp. reads in b nu for ha, and has instead of
our c, d: sapta jy─Бy─Бс╣Б parih┼лta g─Бyaс╣Б saptahot─Б с╣Ыtudayajetit─Бs
sapta gс╣Ыdhr─Б iti ┼Ыu┼Ыrav─Б тАЩhaс╣Б. Nearly all the mss. (all of ours save
E.) read ─Бyam (the saс╣Бhit─Б-mss. -aс╣Б) at end of c.

Griffith

Seven are the Homas, seven the logs for burning, seven are the streams of mead, and seven the seasons. Into the world have come seven streams of butter; those we have heard of as the Seven Vultures.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Seven [are] the meters increasing (-├║ttara) by four, the one set
    upon the other: how do the praises (st├│ma) stand firm in them? how are
    they set in the praises?
Notes

The gender of any├бs at beginning of b speaks strongly for a
compound like the later anyo тАШnya; but the double accent and the
pada-reading (any├бс╕е: any├бsmin) are against it. The pada-text
divides ─Б╠Бrpit─Бni (─Бре░├бrp-) at end of b, but not at end of d.
The verse is wanting in Ppp.

Griffith

Seven metres, by four syllables increasing, each of the seven founded upon another How are the hymns of praise on these supported, and how are these imposed upon the praise-songs?

Whitney
Translation
  1. How did g─Бyatr─л permeate (vi-─Бp) the triple [st├│ma]? how is
    triс╣гс╣н├║bh adapted to that of fifteen? how j─Бgat─л to that of
    thirty-three? how [is] anuс╣гс╣н├║bh that of twenty-one?
Notes

This verse, like the preceding, is wanting in Ppp.; and they are in a
manner interruptions of the progress of the hymn.

Griffith

How hath the Gayatri filled out three triads? On the fifteen how is the Trishtup moulded, Jagati fashioned on the three-and-thirty? How is Anushtup formed? how Ekavinsa?

Translation
  1. Eight [are] born the beings first-born of righteousness; eight, O
    Indra, are the priests (с╣Ыtv├нj) who are of the gods; Aditi has eight
    wombs (y├│ni), eight sons; the oblation (havy├бm) goes unto the eighth
    night.

Griffith

Eight Elements sprang up, first born of Order: the Priests divine are eight in number, Indra! Eight are the wombs of Aditi, eight her children; for the eighth night is the libation destined.

реиреи рдЗрддреНрдердВ рд╢реНрд░реЗрдпреЛ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Thus thinking what is better have I come hither; in your friendship
    I am auspicious (┼Ы├йva); being of the same birth, your skill is
    propitious; it (m.), understanding, goes about to you all (f.).
Notes

The adjectives in a, b are fem., seeming to indicate that the
vir─Бj is regarded as speaking. Ppp. has ─Б тАЩgaс╣Б at end of a, and
nas for vas both times in c, d. ‘It’ in d apparently refers to
‘skill.’

Griffith

So planning bliss for you have I come hither to win your friendship: kind am I, and gracious. Born from one source, propitious is your wisdom: knowing full well to all of you it cometh.

Griffith

To Indra eight, to Yama six, seven to the Rishis, seven to each: The number five accompanies waters and men and healing herbs.

Griffith

The Heifer, all his own, poured forth for Indra control and milk at her first time of milking; And he then satisfied the four divisions, the Gods and men and Asuras and Rishis.

Translation
  1. What now [is] the ox (g├│), who the sole seer, what the abode
    (dh─Б╠Бman), what the blessings (─Б┼Ы├нs)? the monster on the earth [is]
    simple (ekavс╣Ы╠Бt); the sole seasonтАФwhich now is that?
Notes

Ppp. reads s─Бma for dh─Бma in b. All our mss. combine ekaс╣Ыс╣г├нs
in a, but all ekart├║s (also Ppp.) in d. It is necessary here
and in the next verse to render g─Б├║s ‘ox,’ because the accompanying
adjectives are masculine. ‘Which’ in d is the superlative katam├б.

Griffith

Who is the Cow? Who is the Single Rishi? What is the law, what are the benedictions? What on the earth is the one only Spirit? Which of the number is the Single Season?

Whitney
Translation
  1. One [is] the ox, one the sole seer, one the abode, singly the
    blessings; the monster on the earth [is] single; the sole season is
    not in excess.
Notes

Again Ppp. reads s─Бma for dh─Бma, and all the mss. (with Ppp.) have
ekaс╣Ыс╣г├нs but ekart├║s.

тМКHere ends the ninth artha-s┼лkta. It begins with k├║taс╕е. The quoted
Anukr. here says kutaс╕е.тМЛ

Griffith

One is the Cow, one is the Single Spirit, one is the law, single are benedictions. The Spirit dwelling on the earth is single: the Single Season never is transcended.
